## OS hacking: Event loop timers using select()
- **Thumbnail url**: https://i.ytimg.com/vi/gpyKbzzQ8dc/maxresdefault.jpg
- **Channel name**: Andreas Kling
- **Views**: 2131
- **Likes**: 49
- **Comments**: 4
- **Duration in seconds**: 4293
- **Duration in minutes**: 71.55
- **Duration in timestamp**: 1:11:33
- **Duration**: 1 Hours\, 11 Minutes\, 33 Seconds
- **Uploaded Time**: 2019\-02\-02T03:01:03
- **Video url**: https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=gpyKbzzQ8dc
- **Tags**: [#os hacking, #os development, #kernel development, #kernel hacking, #vt100, #terminal, #terminal emulation, #terminal development, #serenity os, #c++, #c++ hacking, #c++ development, #make your own operating system, #make your own os, #make your own kernel, #operating system hacking, #operating system development, #operating system programming, #c++ programming]
- **Tags (in description)**: []
- **Emails (in description)**: []
- **Links (in description)**: [https://github.com/awesomekling/serenity]
- **Description**: In this video I implement a GUI event loop timer using the select\(\) system call\. Since select\(\) didn't support arbitrary timeouts in Serenity\, I also implement support for that in the kernel\. I realized after recording this video that the solution for millisecond accuracy in gettimeofday\(\) isn't good enough\, and will work on that in a later patch\.
    
    Recorded on 2019\-02\-01\.
    
    Serenity is a 32\-bit Unix\-like operating system I'm implementing from scratch\, just for fun\. https://github\.com/awesomekling/serenity
